### Post by onefish2 on 2008-10-27
As far as i can tell the image that Dell posted on their site is NOT the same as the RESTORE DVD that comes with the Mini9.

I have a copy of that restore DVD. It boots into a graphical environment that asks if you want to do a restore.

I finally got the img that is posted on the Dell support site to run from a USB key. There are two ways to do this. Since its an image NOT an iso you can use the "dd" command. It would look like this:

sudo dd if=/path_to_restore_image/restore_image.img of=/path_to_your_USB_key bs=1024

The other way is to download image-writer
[http://ppa.launchpad.net/ogra/ubuntu/pool/main/u/usb-imagewriter/usb-imagewriter_0.1-1~ppa1_all.deb](http://ppa.launchpad.net/ogra/ubuntu/pool/main/u/usb-imagewriter/usb-imagewriter_0.1-1~ppa1_all.deb)

image-writer is a graphical front end for dd. Look for it in Applications/Accessories

I booted off the USB key to a text based screen advising me that if I press enter the system would be over written with the restore image. The system was restored and it asked you to remove the USB key. Then the system was rebooted.

I went through the initial set up and after another reboot. It was up and running the Dell version of Ubuntu Hardy.

Problem solved.

---

### Post by jdawdy on 2008-10-30
Just FYI, I can confirm that the Mini 9 works with SDHC cards.  I have a 16GB adata brand Class 6 SDHC turbo card which works no problem.  Mpeg video plays fine off of it (I wanted to be sure that I could store movies on the card for playback).

I preferred to spend my money on the SD card as opposed to ordering the dell with 16GB of memory, as there is not much difference in the price and the card is more flexible as a removable drive.

### Post by feranick on 2008-10-30
> **benlen said:**
> I am (trying) to download the dell mini OS from [ftp://ftp.us.dell.com/OS/Inspiron_910_Ubuntu_A00.img](ftp://ftp.us.dell.com/OS/Inspiron_910_Ubuntu_A00.img)

Will this Dell mini OS be updated automatically when 8.10 are released today, or will I be stuck with hardy?

I tried Ubuntu netbook remix but not sure if I liked it. Is the dell mini OS better? Or should I just go for a (Vanilla) 8.10? Maybe xubuntu?

No. The 8.04.1 in the mini is a custom version of the Ubuntu Desktop, it doesn't use ubuntu official repositories. Thus you won't see any upgrade invitation. 

In general Dell moves to the current Ubuntu distro after a few months it has been released by Canonical. They want to make sure it works well on their systems.

One question: What's wrong with 8.04.1? It works perfectly in the mini, and I honestly don't see any reason for upgrading. OpenOffice is still 2.4.1, and other than that there is very little incentive to go through an unsupported (do-it-yourself) upgrade. Besides, 8.04 is a long term release.

### Post by dcaulton on 2008-10-31

I saw via 'df' that I had only 4GB, but I was already attached to the machine and am naturally wary of any nonessential mail-in repairs.  I would have settled for a refund on the upgrade since I really wanted more than 16GB anyway, but the situation resolved itself before I got around to calling tech support.

About a week ago, Dell pushed an update that fixed the partition problem.  It was nice and seamless and I give them credit for taking care of it in the way they did.  I can try and dig more information out of my logs if you want, but I've scanned this thread and I don't think I've seen any mention of that.  

I like the mini 9 for what it is.  It's a great secondary machine for browsing and other light tasks, but I'm not even really considering using it for virtualization, or running a LAMP stack, or (more to my interests) using it as a digital recording station.  The fact is, this is just about the cheapest, lowest powered new laptop one can buy - my gut tells me that there will always be some bottleneck in the hardware if you try and make it act like a regular laptop.

### Post by yakker.yak on 2008-11-07
> **RichTJ99 said:**
> Mine shipped & should be to me tomorrow afternoon.  Of course I am heading out of town for the weekend & Fedex will need to deliver it on Monday. 

Either way, I was curious if I cant get Crossover or Virtual Box working, my only option is to try to install 8.10 to have the .deb files?

There's a short guide to re-packaging a 386 deb to an lpia one. It's for skype but the general idea applies to any third-party deb:
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6058820#post6058820](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6058820#post6058820)

In essense, you just need to change the architecture field in the deb and re-package. This is a better route than using dpkg --force since it enables you to manage and uninstall the packages easily within synaptic.

BTW, Crossover also has a command-line installer that should work on most platforms, regardless of the distribution.

### Post by yakker.yak on 2008-11-07

The LAN interface works great. I was able to do an update to see if that fixed the WAN interface, but no luck.

Hmm, lots of variables really.

Have you tried connecting to your router with the encryption turned off (i.e. no WEP or WPA)?

Have you tried it with another router (i.e. coffee shop)?

It'd be good to know if the problem persists across different configurations. If that's the case, then you may have a problem with your WAN card which may need to be replaced/serviced.

### Post by Sunspark on 2008-11-09
Hi folks!

(This is a mini-review/commentary.)

My gf replaced her EEE 701 with the Mini 9. She ordered it with the Windows version because it was slightly on sale. I requested that she also add the bluetooth and 16 gb drive options. It already came with 1 GB ram as part of the package.

It was horrifically slow. Reason was because of the compressed NTFS drive. Un-compressing it made it a bit better. But neither she or I are Windows fans.

I blew away the partition and installed the 8.10 i386 flavours of ubuntu, kubuntu, and xubuntu to try out because it had been a long time for me since I played in Linux (I use OS X) and I wanted to see how they are now.

-Suspend works just fine in ubuntu, you need to select 'suspend' in the gnome power manager preferences, and then you can open and close the lid all you want.

-I had no problems with WIFI. I let it use the closed source STA driver. I didn't test with the b43 oss driver that is also an option on the 8.10 disc. I believe the oss driver will continue to mature and will toss out the STA driver eventually. Broadcom is not oss friendly.

-The brightness and sound keys work fine, no special config needed.

-The mini9 can run Virtualbox fine. I had to poke at it a bit, but it runs XP and Office just fine. (Not even going to try games.) The reason this was necessary is because apparently Office 2007 has a very good bibliography and citation manager, and it doesn't appear in anything else that she was aware of.. OO's is broken. Something for them to work on I suppose for the future.

-Be aware to change virtualbox's preferences for mode switching before you run it, there is no right ctrl-key.

-There is no F11 or F12, maybe a future bios will assign it to the Z and X keys. Depending on your program you may need to remap some F keys to get the F11 and F12 keys back. I haven't yet worked with remapping keys.. if I did the first thing I'd do would be to switch the ' key which they placed on the spacebar row, with the the ; key which remains in it's original spot.

-I was amused to discover that the Mini 9 can be converted into a Hackintosh. I did not test this.

-The STEC 16 gb drive while fast enough at reads, only really writes at about 12 mb/s. It reads fine. For what the mini9 will be used for, 12 mb/s is acceptable. I read that the 4 and 8 gb versions are even slower at writes. Do not buy those. or if you do, remove the drive and replace them with one of your own (like Intel's SSD).

-I hated the new electronics smell of the mini 9. It is strong. It'll go away in time (1-3 months, might linger longer as there is no fan to exhaust the interior), but blech.

-I found myself being bemused that while backlight is LED, I remember reading that one of the 'advantages' of LED over CFL is that on areas of large black, it will selectively turn off specific LEDs to make it blacker.  I have never seen anyone do it, and this panel does not do that. There is always 'backlight glow' even on a black screen. There is also no function key ability to turn the backlight off like on the Macs, has to be done using software.

-I found myself noticing that 
-Kubuntu really pissed me off. It was buggy, and this was unfortunate because KDE was her request as she is used to it. There is graphical garble on the screen behind the KDE window on the login screen, and there were issues with it loading multiple wireless driver systray applets, etc. when more than 1 desktop was loaded. Also, I failed at getting it to connect to the school's wireless network and had to give up. Maybe a clean install would have been better. KDE is pretty, but no cookie for now.

-I wish I had noticed this earlier as I have to return the machine to her today, but XFCE is fast! If you have a mini 9, I really do recommend you install Xubuntu instead of the other 2 flavours. Dare I say it? But Xubuntu actually has a wee bit of 'teh snappy'. Gnome is slower in comparison. Save yourself some annoyance and go with Xubuntu if you want speed. If you want even more speed and have some time and ability, use a window manager and forget about the desktop. But by all means try XFCE. I was quite impressed, and it's currently installed as a dual session with Gnome and she can pick what she likes. But I know now that I'd be using XFCE if it was my machine.

-I noticed that installing multiple flavours causes all 3 flavours to install their apps and so forth in the menus of each other. This, I did not like. I understand why this was done, but it is 'messy'. So be aware of this.

-I think for better looking fonts, one needs to switch the system from the bytecode interpreter, to the autohinter. After doing this, have subpixel and slight hinting selected. (dpkgfontconfig-config in the cli, and then after dpkgfontconfig to rebuild caches)

-I installed the 'preload' daemon to get a bit of extra speed.

-For more speed I also:
  -changed /tmp to ram instead of disk (fstab)
  -switched the cfq scheduler to noop due to ssd nature of the drive (menu.lst)
  -moved the firefox browser cache to ram. (about : options).

Well that's it! Hope this was of use to someone.

---

### Post by cyclist23 on 2008-11-10
> **RichTJ99 said:**
> This might be a bunch of basic questions (or two), as I type from my new mini (I LOVE THIS THING), 

1.  What is the Dell installed Netmix  is that the quick launch on the home screen?  

2.  Using the Dell Lpia vs a standard 8.10 install - Does all the hardware work in 8.10  does suspend work?  

3.  How much faster is the Dell Ubuntu vs the 8.10 standard?y 

4.  Are there any links to precompiled Lpia (Skype, etc)?

Thanks,
Rich

2. Suspend works just fine in 8.10

3. Noticeably faster.  The tradeoff is the full Ubuntu with all the latest packages, or a limited Ubuntu with older version to most packages and some not available at all.  Don't worry about the 886MB of RAM limit on the Dell Ubuntu.  Even though it recognizes only 886MB of RAM it is still faster than 8.10 with 2GB of RAM.

---

### Post by emptythevoid on 2008-11-12
> **silverh20 said:**
> by the way, anyone know why flash video playback is so poor? i have yet to try a regular file off the ssd.

I think the issue is more to do with Adobe's Flash, rather than the computer itself.  I've got a dual core Lenovo Thinkpad with 2GB of ram and dedicated 256MB nVidia graphics card, and even with that, running Ubuntu, flash within the browser sometimes hiccups.  However, if I download the FLV files to the computer and play them back on Totem or VLC, even on my 7 year old 900Mhz Panasonic Toughbook, playback is much much better.  Let me say, though, that this is purely anecdotal.  I'm no expert.

### Post by 2damncommon on 2008-11-12
Type "http://archive.ubuntu.com" in your browser. Click on "ubuntu", click on "dists", click on "hardy", click on "main", now notice a problem, there is no "binary-lpia" directory. Apparently the hard rather than hardy was a posting error. I do not know what other sources you added but they point to nothing AFAICS.

I am guessing your /etc/apt/sources.list contains the same addresses you posted in the thumbnail.

My /etc/apt/sources.list contains:
deb [http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/](http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/) hardy main universe multiverse restricted
deb-src [http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/](http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/) hardy main universe multiverse restricted

deb [http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/](http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/) hardy-updates main universe multiverse restricted
deb-src [http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/](http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/) hardy-updates main universe multiverse restricted

deb [http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/](http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/) hardy-security main universe multiverse restricted
deb-src [http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/](http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/) hardy-security main universe multiverse restricted

deb [http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/](http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/) hardy-netbook-base main universe multiverse restricted
deb-src [http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/](http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/) hardy-netbook-base main universe multiverse restricted

deb [http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/](http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/) hardy-dell-mini main universe multiverse restricted
deb-src [http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/](http://dell-mini.archive.canonical.com/ubuntu/) hardy-dell-mini main universe multiverse restricted

Edit your /etc/apt/sources.list as needed.

### Post by jdawdy on 2008-11-13
Go to System>Administration>Software sources

Make sure all the boxes under the Ubuntu Software tab are UNchecked.

Make sure all the boxes under third party software tab are CHECKED,

Click on close, and just to be sure open Update Manager.  Should be all up to date.

---

### Post by onefish2 on 2008-11-13

Rich

I would google for how to use the dd command to write out the iso to a usb drive. In the mean time this may be the exact command.

Would be something like this:

dd if=/path-to-iso/disc.iso of=/dev/sdb bs-1024

Assuming sdb is your unmounted USB drive.

Sorry about that it should be bs=1024.

dd if=/home/rich/mini9.iso of=/dev/sdb bs=1024

Make sure /dev/sdb is really your usb drive.

### Post by gregconquest on 2008-11-16
> **RichTJ99 said:**
> BTW, has anyone been able to get a bootable USB drive to get Clonezilla launched?  I keep getting an error saying:

BUG:  soft lockup - CPU#0 stuck for 61s![kmemstick:2351]

This gets stuck in a loop.

Is it just me?

What version of CloneZilla are you using? I tried both a USB flash drive and a CD in a USB DVD drive, and neither one worked.

Error message:
```
BOOT FAILED!
This Debian Live image failed to boot.

Please file a bug against the 'live-initramfs' package or email the Debian Live mailing list at <debian-live@lists.debian.org>, making sure to note the exact version, name and distribution of the image you were attempting to boot.

The file /live.log contains some debugging information but booting with the debug command-line parameter will greatly increase its verbosity which is extremely useful when diagnosing issues.

live-initramfs will now start a shell. The error message was:

Unable to find a medium containing a live file system

BusyBox v1.1.3 (Debian 1:1.1.3-4) Built-in shell (ash)
Enter 'help' for a list of built-in commands.

/bin/sh: can't access tty; job control turned off
(initramfs) 
```

This error is from booting a CDR of CloneZilla live 1.2.0-25 on an as-yet otherwise unbooted mini 9 with a 16GB SSD. 

I filed a bug report and then checked to see if CloneZilla had been updated (I should have checked first, but I just downloaded CloneZilla in September...). And voila, yes. There was a new version 1.2.1-17 (2008-11-13 02:31):
[http://clonezilla.org/download/sourceforge/]("http://clonezilla.org/download/sourceforge/")

I downloaded and burned a new CD and it worked fine. I haven't tried the USB flash drive again yet.

Greg

### Post by gregconquest on 2008-11-16
**[COLOR="Red"]Problem Solved -- Update at bottom of this message.[/COLOR]**

I'm still in the early stages of configuring my mini 9 (ubuntu), but I've encountered one irritating problem already. There is an extra tab in my "**web browser**" that goes to **an ad by CoreComm** ("www.en.com/#").

This is not listed in in my home page (Edit -- Preferences -- Main -- Home Page). So, **where could it be?** A search for this turns up lots of hits but very little of relevancy.

Thanks for any help.
Greg Conquest

keys: DELL spyware pop-up advertisement spam commercial bloatware

**UPDATE:**

I have found the source of this problem. I had entered three pages as my home page with one of them being google's translation page (Japanese to English, in this case). Here is the link, and the problem:
[http://translate.google.com/translate_t?langpair=ja|en#]("http://translate.google.com/translate_t?langpair=ja|en#")

The &#8220;|&#8221; character separates the "ja" and the "en" (Japanese to English), but Firefox uses that character to separate url's in its list of home pages. So, Firefox saw one of my home pages as being "en#" and loaded "www.en.com/#" as a result.

---

### Post by feranick on 2008-11-18
> **RainyCity said:**
> 
I'm running the Dell netbook remix OS and every time I open a new window it defaults to full screen. For Firefox that is fine but the Firefox download window as well as file browser windows default to full screen. The annoying bit is that if I resize them and close them when I open them again the pop back to full screen. Is there a way to disable this?


It's because of "maximus" a program for the mini that by default brings the window to full size. To disable it:

1. System -> Preferences -> Sessions

2. Uncheck maximus.

3. restart X (or reboot).


Be aware that this will also disable the full screen (in the proper sense) activation by the "windows" button.

---

### Post by yakker.yak on 2008-11-20
Came across [this]("https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/network-manager-applet/+bug/284211"), which suggests that PEAP with GTC is in fact supported by Network Manager in 8.04, but not 8.10 (hence the bug).

BTW, are you testing the right settings: is PEAP with EAP-MSCHAP v2 not different from PEAP with GTC?

### Post by feranick on 2008-11-23
> **Andorien said:**
> This may well be a stupid question, but here goes:

Since the installation this thing ships with is a special dell remix of 8.04, can I easily upgrade it to 8.10 via the package manager like normal, or would I have to do a fresh, non-remix installation?

The ubuntu mini 8.04 uses special repositories, so you won't be able to upgrade to 8.10 using the package manager. 

If you need for some reason 8.10, you may find how [here]("http://www.ubuntumini.com/2008/10/ubuntu-810-intrepid-ibex-on-dell-mini-9.html").

### Post by JC Cheloven on 2008-11-29
Hi, 

I'm proud to inform the community that Dell Mini 9 [is sold as Ubuntu-only in Spain]("http://www1.euro.dell.com/content/products/productdetails.aspx/laptop-inspiron-9?c=es&cs=esdhs1&l=es&s=dhs") :-)

It can be purchased at [some major stores]("http://www.carrefouronline.carrefour.es/noalimentacion/NodoTerminal.aspx?itemId=cat930004&pila=catalog310026@cat410364@cat930004&menu=yes&navCount=0&&itemMarcado=catalog310026&nivel_desplegado=nivel2_4")  for 299&#8364;. Unfortunately I paid 19&#8364; more as I ordered mine a month ago at Dell store (hurry is never good).

I have it for 5 days now. Everything works out of the box: Wireless, sound, webcam, card reader... Not even a single problem! Now I find myself missing that feeling of endlessly hacking my system in order to deserve using it :-D  It just works, this time for true.

Of course I'll install intrepid soon, as I miss running into problems :-)  Forgive me, I'm a bit too excited :lolflag:

Just in case someone missed it: [here]("http://www.ubuntumini.com/") is a lot of useful info.

Greetings :guitar:

Nope. I've been using the Mini for a few weeks now and if I had to settle for only one laptop this wouldn't be it. Don't get me wrong, I love my Mini, but to have it as my only production machine it would be frustrating. In 2 to 3 years buy yourself an even better netbook for less money and don't share it with the kids. You deserve it. :)

### Post by yakker.yak on 2008-12-01

I think it's quite reasonable. Have had my Mini9 for over two weeks now and it's my primary PC: docked to a monitor and USB keyboard/mouse when I work at a desk, otherwise great battery life and silent when it's unplugged.

It should be perfect for college, provided your daughter doesn't do any serious gaming :) But for email, web, Office, it's more than enough CPU, RAM, hard drive, etc. There's a 32GB version now as well. Rather than invest in an extra hard drive for music and video, could also use that money and buy a portable music/media player.

Unfortunately, may be difficult to get by without an external CD/DVD drive both to install software and/or to save music/videos ... I do have one of these and it's pretty handy.

### Post by JC Cheloven on 2008-12-01

> The Dell Mini 9 includes a VGA port I believe.  How good is the graphics card for resolutions?

I have a 20" widescreen monitor and wondered if this would work with the Mini 9 (combined with a USB keyboard/mouse ) as a sort-of dock and then unplug when its time to go? I also have 2 CRT non-ws monitors if the ratio messes things up.

Among other things, I'm using the mini 9 to watch movies in my 32 inch TV screen. [INDENT]--> Why? well, I have a multimedia HD which sucks. Won't play many of my movies because of the format or resolution. The mini 9 does, and the vga output makes it perfect.[/INDENT]
I have to say that the quality is ok. We didn't notice a difference between a playback from the Multimedia Disk and from the mini9. Or if any, would be in favour of the mini9.

It's not exactly your question, but I hope this gives you an idea.

EDIT: Out of curiosity, I've just tried for you the mini 9 with the 22 inch monitor of my main computer, and a usb flexible keyboard. Everything smooth. If you connect the monitor after boot, a big image of the mini9 screen appears in the monitor (fitted in height). If you boot with the monitor connected, the resolution adjusts as suitable for the monitor, and the mini9 screen shows as much as it fits of the upper right corner of the monitor. Smooth as a charm :-)

### Post by solitaire on 2008-12-04
don't worry [greenleaves123]("http://ubuntuforums.org/member.php?u=721496") :D just search and have a nosey around these forums and ask questions, were here to help! :D

As for the Mini 9.

32Gb is loads of space when it comes to Linux. If you are using it for Word Processing, surfing and emails then that will last you for ages! but to be safe pick up a SD card to copy / backup important files and to swap things between your Desktop and the laptop. :D

Ubuntu only looks complex because you are used to Windows, but give it a week or 2 of playing around and you should find it just as easy as your desktop. Best thing you can do is play around with it before you get anything important on it! 

Learn and make mistakes when you've got nothing on it to lose :D

### Post by feranick on 2008-12-05
Did anybody notice that no updates have been pushed for the Ubuntu for the mini. Packages are old (Firefox is still in version 3.0.3), outdated and full with vulnerabilities. I filed a bug for this:

[https://bugs.launchpad.net/dell-mini/+bug/301489](https://bugs.launchpad.net/dell-mini/+bug/301489)

for which (as for all other bugs) there hasn't been any word from developers.
I posted the issue in ideastorm:

[http://www.ideastorm.com/ideaView?id=087700000000ECdAAM](http://www.ideastorm.com/ideaView?id=087700000000ECdAAM)

As is, the mini is definitively unsafe to use. I am amazed to notice that nobody actually raise this problem up, or even care. I think dell/canonical should do a much better job in maintaining this custom distro....

I would recommend the users to be more vocal about this issue, and to let their voice heard.

### Post by jsonder on 2008-12-13
You can download the 3.1 beta 2 version here:

[http://www.mozilla.com/en-US/firefox/all-beta.html](http://www.mozilla.com/en-US/firefox/all-beta.html)

Open it with the archive manage and select "extract".

And yes, it does yield 2 installations.  I removed the existing firefox icon, and put an icon on the desktop for the new beta2.  That keeps it simple for me.

---

### Post by feranick on 2008-12-14
> **runningdoc said:**
> For new users, do I go to the website for Firefox and download the latest version and will it overwrite the version I have?  With the update feature still work through the update manager if and when they update the repositories?  Thank you for your help.

The new version will sit besides your existing one. The update system in the new one will most likely work. However I will be a bit careful in having two very different version installed.

Both will use the same profile, with your configuration files. Going back and forth with the two version is usually not a good idea, since it can create instabilities. So at least you should backup you profile folder (/home/USER/.mozilla).

---

### Post by bpl07 on 2008-12-14
If you want to use firefox 3.1b2, I would suggest adding an ubuntu ppa in Software Sources for it and installing it through synaptic package manager.  The ppa I use is:

[https://launchpad.net/~fta/+archive](https://launchpad.net/~fta/+archive)

There's a lot of other goodies in there too.  Installing this way avoids mixing profiles and will be easier to upgrade when the official release is out.

---

### Post by runningdoc on 2008-12-14
Thank you for the explanation and for everyone expanding on this.  It has helped to make the installation work easier.

### Post by RainyCity on 2008-12-17
> **RainyCity said:**
> Posted bug to Launchpad.
  [https://bugs.launchpad.net/dell-mini/+bug/300784](https://bugs.launchpad.net/dell-mini/+bug/300784)
Just an update that this wireless problem is solved.

The wl kernel module in the Dell Mini 9 was unable to support WPA2 Enterprise, PEAP, MSCHAPv2 wireless networks. I ended up going old school and using ndiswrapper with a downloaded driver and it works fine.

I used the excellent instructions found here, steps 1, 2e, and 3.
  [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/WifiDocs/Driver/bcm43xx/Feisty_No-Fluff](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/WifiDocs/Driver/bcm43xx/Feisty_No-Fluff)

I'll be updating the bug report with more detail but the takeaway is that the wl driver is pretty good but if you run into trouble go with ndiswrapper.

---

### Post by ArKay on 2008-12-29
I reinstalled from the, well, restore DVD. No hassle, just bang, zoom and all set to go.  The codecs, as far as I can tell, are installed with the OS using the restore DVD for Ubuntu. There was no need for the drivers DVD that I could find. After doing the restore everything worked fine. When I installed 8.10 to a different ssd on the other hand the codecs weren't there. :( But I never got the chance to poke around the drivers disk since it seemed rather windows oriented. (see below)

On the other hand, if you go to install Windows (say if you were going to dual boot from one of the 32 GB M.D.D. ssds ) you need the drivers DVD to set up all the hardware that Windows has _no_ idea about what to do with.

But regardless, I didn't have a problem using an old external DVD drive and restoring by rebooting, choosing the DVD as my boot device and telling it to go at it.

I will see if I can get a chance to poke around the drivers DVD and see if there are Ubuntu codecs on it or if it's just the windows stuff.

---

### Post by ArKay on 2008-12-29
And I am (fairly) certain it is indeed simply the Windows resource disk.

And the autorun.bat and the English documentation on the DVD pretty much confirm this. To me at least.

If there are codecs hiding on there, they are probably compressed and designed to be installed, into Windows (95, 98, ME, XP, 2000, NT, 2003 Server) according to the .ini files hiding on there.

Now, I'm no major league hacker - I lost all that round about Windows 3.11... Maybe someone could find them by running through the .iso of the restore disk or some woe begotten spot on the Drivers Disk, but it is _way_ beyond my humble Linux talents. Rusty as they are from the days of Shell Internet Access - when Pine, Lynx and actual terminal commands ruled the day. And even then, I only knew enough to get along. Now with the rise of GUIs my Linux-fu is sad. :sad:

### Post by magicfab on 2008-12-30
Anyone owning a Mini 9 should take a good look at this wiki page:
[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/DellMini9](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/DellMini9)

It lists common issues for the Mini 9 with Ubuntu, either pre-installed from factory or installed from an Ubuntu vanilla 8.04.1 CD.

It also has direct links to the documentation that came with the computer in electronic form, as well as links to other community sites, forums and mailing lists.

If you have a specific question about the Mini 9, it is also possible to ask it here:
[https://answers.launchpad.net/dell-mini/+addquestion](https://answers.launchpad.net/dell-mini/+addquestion)

I can't answer all questions here in the forum, but I keep a close eye on questions asked via Launchpad.

Thank you.

### Post by emptythevoid on 2009-01-10
I'm having a very unusual problem with my Mini 9 that I bought from the Dell (Refurb) Outlet store the other day.  I got my Mini preloaded with Dell's Ubunti 8.04, but I immediately installed 8.10 - I know that this isn't officially supported by Dell, but I've been reading and it seems that plenty of other people have been using it with minimal issues.  But I don't think my problem is entirely software-related, so just tell me what you guys think.

Often, when the computer is restarted, shut down, or put into suspend, the sound won't work when the computer is back online.  Now I know there's a sound fix for 8.10 (editing the modprobe.d/alsa-base) and I did that, and it worked.  For a while.  The sound will work, but then after a suspend (for example), no sound after waking.  What I get is an audible "click" when I toggle the mute/unmute button (or keystroke), and i can still hear the systembeep.  but no other sound.  

Once the sound stops working, rebooting or shutting down the computer does not *necessarily* fix it.  Here's what I mean.  I'll have the laptop on, with sound working, and then i'll put it into standby.  Wake it back up, sound doesn't work.  Immediately put it into standby again.  Wake it back up.  Sometimes the sound will resume working, sometimes it won't.  it's the same whether i put it into standby, reboot it, or shut it down.  Tried removing the battery and unplugging it.  The sound still continues to only work when it feels like working. 

I went into the BIOS (version A00 - have not tried updating it) and disabled the bluetooth.  This *seems* so far to fix the audio problem, but strangely the Wireless is no longer available.  I know this is odd, and I double-checked to make sure that i didn't accidentally disable the WLAN instead of the bluetooth.  I also tried re-installing 8.10 and also booting up using a LiveUSB stick with 8.10 and the same problems occurred both times (and yes, I made the adjustment to the alsa-base on the USB stick)

I've been watching the forums since before the mini 9 came out, looking for early adopter hardware problems, and I haven't seen anything like this.  Think maybe I just got a defect?  After all, it was "previously ordered new" refurbished.

I've already e-mailed Dell's Tech Support with the intention of returning it and getting an exchange or something, but I really wanted to hear what you guys have to say, since it seems like an unusual issue.  Thanks so much (sorry this was so lengthy)!

---

### Post by jsonder on 2009-01-10
Running on line power, I can have rhythmbox playing and after suspending, it continues playing upon being restarted (did it twice).  I have Bluetooth unchecked (in preferences-sessions) as well as the Gnome startup sound and all of the tracker stuff.  Oh, I'm also using wicd instead of the 8.10 network manager.  I did a suspend and then went to youtube without problems.

So, I can't reproduce your problem using line power.  

Also, I made a real pest of myself asking Dell's tech support folk if the bios upgrade was needed.  I was told that the upgrade (from A00) was not recommended.

### Post by emptythevoid on 2009-01-14
Well, here's the update:

I installed the Dell Ubuntu 8.04 image from the website.  It installed just fine, and sound worked just after the install.  But as soon as I suspended it and woke it back up, the problem returned:  No sound, and just a clicky sound out of the speakers when toggling mute/unmute.  Sound did not restore after a shutdown.

I even tried the plain ol' vanilla 8.04.1 and that didn't help either.  So I guess I'll be calling Dell tech support and convincing them they need to take a look at it.

UPDATE:  Since the factory restore put the Dell Diagnostic partition on the drive, I ran a test while on the phone with Dell.  The laptop failed the Audio test with an error code:  1B63:0268 and the message:  AUDIO - codec failed to generate interrupts.

So Dell's sending me an empty box and I'm going to be getting a new motherboard and speakers.  Hopefully it'll come back all better - I really love the little guy.

Maybe try to format your usb flash drive to fat16 instead and see if it'll fix your problem. kind of weird. i thought fat16 and fat 32 are the same.

btw, sometimes my sound mutes too. If two programs make a sound at the same time. Usually a restart will fix it. I think its a on according bug that isn't fix yet.

Well, if the Dell diagnostic partition is reporting problems with the motherboard, then I don't think the file system on the flash drive's going to matter.

And the problem you're referring to, about multiple applications now playing sound simultaneously, is a PulseAudio problem (going to the sound preferences and setting everything to use ALSA, and *then* going in to your video or sound programs and forcing them to *also* use ALSA pretty much fixed that for me).  My problem wasn't like that.  The sound would continue to not operate even *after* a restart, without any programs open.  The sound test function in the sound preferences wouldn't work.  So I'm pretty sure it's hardware-related, but we'll see. :)

### Post by klange on 2009-01-20
> **ugm6hr said:**
> Sorry for the question - but a description of how to do this wouold be useful.

I'd like to give it a try to see if it actually makes a difference.  My 2D performance seems fine - but I'm not sure what the "norm" is for this hardware.
You won't notice the speed issues under Metacity, but with Compiz, scrolling in Firefox is quite slow.

Anyway, the fix is simple and has to do with an update that was made that changed the defaults for X.

```
sudo nano /etc/X11/xorg.conf
```
Find the "Device" section. Add this:
```
Section "Device"
        Identifier      "Configured Video Device"
        Option          "FrameBufferCompression"        "false"
        **Option          "AccelMethod"   "xaa"**
EndSection
```
(Optionally add the FrameBufferCompression line, it'll make Compiz faster, but may cause a 5-minute loss of battery life.)

Come to think of it, it may just be lack of any acceleration. I should try using EXA explicitly. (I always preferred XAA until it stopped working in Intrepid, though...)

**e**: Another thing: If you have red window borders, it's because bg[SELECTED] is only using red pixels in Metacity. You can hack in hex values for colors in an alternate copy of your decorations. I just replaced all of the calls to anything bg[SELECTED], ignoring shading rules (so while not perfect, my windows are at least the right colors), as I wasn't sure if the shading had something to do with it. Meh, have fun.

---

### Post by Craigacp on 2009-01-22
> **WindowsSucks said:**
> You won't notice the speed issues under Metacity, but with Compiz, scrolling in Firefox is quite slow.

Anyway, the fix is simple and has to do with an update that was made that changed the defaults for X.

```
sudo nano /etc/X11/xorg.conf
```
Find the "Device" section. Add this:
```
Section "Device"
        Identifier      "Configured Video Device"
        Option          "FrameBufferCompression"        "false"
        **Option          "AccelMethod"   "xaa"**
EndSection
```
(Optionally add the FrameBufferCompression line, it'll make Compiz faster, but may cause a 5-minute loss of battery life.)

Come to think of it, it may just be lack of any acceleration. I should try using EXA explicitly. (I always preferred XAA until it stopped working in Intrepid, though...)

**e**: Another thing: If you have red window borders, it's because bg[SELECTED] is only using red pixels in Metacity. You can hack in hex values for colors in an alternate copy of your decorations. I just replaced all of the calls to anything bg[SELECTED], ignoring shading rules (so while not perfect, my windows are at least the right colors), as I wasn't sure if the shading had something to do with it. Meh, have fun.

I was having a dig around in the forums for the intel hardy driver (because my graphics felt sluggish) and if you export INTEL_BATCH=1 (by adding the line to /etc/environment) then it almost doubles the glxgears performance from on average 505fps 

2535 frames in 5.0 seconds = 506.890 FPS

to around 980fps

4943 frames in 5.0 seconds = 988.437 FPS.

According to what I read in the dev for the intel ubuntu driver this doesn't cause any problems with the 945 chipset in the dell mini 9.

Edit:

Adding 
Option "ExaNoComposite" "false"
Option "MigrationHeuristic" "greedy"
made firefox back to its usual nippy self, and it now runs the window picker scale thingy faster than my core 2 duo desktop (though that has a high res screen, and a much greater number of windows open).

Also I should note i'm using:
Option          "AccelMethod"   "exa"

### Post by billcondie on 2009-03-01
Just got my Mini 9 with 4G SSD.

Not enough space to install Wine.

What's the downside of a clean install without the Dell/Yahoo crap?

Also, I upgraded to 2G RAM. How big a Swap file. Obviously not 6G! 

Advice appreciated before I blunder ahead.

---

### Post by Rallg on 2009-03-01
My unit is a machine that came with XP. Eventually I did dual-boot, then eventually eliminated XP (not that I hate Windows, but all my software was Linux stuff ported to Windows). I have the 16G SSD, but I can tell you this:

I have not had a problem by installing 8.10 directly from the Ubuntu distribution. Do not install an earlier version.

When you install, do NOT use swap. A RAM of 2Gb is more than sufficient for anything that you would be likely to do with this kind of machine. (That is, if 2Gb is not enough for you, then you really need some other technology.) Solid-state drive tolerates fewer write cycles than does a hard drive. Swap activities can use a lot of write cycles. When you install, you will be warned that you did not choose a swap partition. No problem.

If there is a small FAT partition on the drive, it contains Dell diagnostic software. I removed mine, but it might be a good idea to leave it in place if you have it. In any case, having a small FAT partition can be useful if you need to update the BIOS.

After installation, review the distro software. It may be that there is some stuff you don't need, and some of it can take up a lot of space. If the main menu add/remove is refused, you can use Synaptic package manager via adminstrative menu.

With only 4Gb of storage, you will probably have to use a USB or slot card to store your non-system big stuff.

---

### Post by ugm6hr on 2009-03-01
@billcondie:
1. No swap required
2. You can just remove the Yahoo crap rather than reinstalling
3. You can remove almost every application (except Evolution) if you need the space
4. Consider using a separate SD card for storing files.  In theory, you should be able to move /home to the SD card using a LiveUSB (reliable source, but I have never tried): [http://www.psychocats.net/ubuntu/separatehome](http://www.psychocats.net/ubuntu/separatehome)
5. If you do reinstall, consider using an SD card for /home (and perhaps other directories too).

---

### Post by sirebral on 2009-03-01
> **billcondie said:**
> Just got my Mini 9 with 4G SSD.

Not enough space to install Wine.

What's the downside of a clean install without the Dell/Yahoo crap?

Also, I upgraded to 2G RAM. How big a Swap file. Obviously not 6G! 

Advice appreciated before I blunder ahead.

If you do a clean install I would recommend taking a look at Xubuntu.  It is a really small foot print and you have a small SSD.

You don't need to do a clean install to remove the Dell / Yahoo crap.  Don't forget Adobe, Games, anything else that is not being used.  You are not going to lose performance.  You are going to gain some HD space.  Not much, maybe .5 - 1 GB.

---

### Post by Mu. on 2009-03-02
In a terminal type:
sudo apt-get install ubuntu-restricted-extras

If that doesn't sort you out you might try this:

[http://www.ubuntumini.com/2008/10/medibuntu-multimedia-entertainment.html](http://www.ubuntumini.com/2008/10/medibuntu-multimedia-entertainment.html)

### Post by Dragonbite on 2009-03-02
> **billcondie said:**
> Just got my Mini 9 with 4G SSD.

Not enough space to install Wine.

What's the downside of a clean install without the Dell/Yahoo crap?

Also, I upgraded to 2G RAM. How big a Swap file. Obviously not 6G! 

Advice appreciated before I blunder ahead.

I have a laptop running around 1.4 GHz with 512 MB of Ram and barely use any swap space so 2 GB should be ample (unless you are rendering 3D objects in Blender, but I doubt you'd be doing that on a Mini).

For space considerations you may even want to look at using an Alternate CD and only install the applications you want. Removing applications usually leave some crumbs behind.

### Post by emptythevoid on 2009-03-06
> **Rallg said:**
> 
If there is a small FAT partition on the drive, it contains Dell diagnostic software. I removed mine, but it might be a good idea to leave it in place if you have it. In any case, having a small FAT partition can be useful if you need to update the BIOS.


Just my thoughts about the Dell Diagnostics - leave them be.  I bought my Mini 9 from the refurb outlet and it immediately had a hardware problem.  The Dell diagnostics ran a check and was able to identify the problem and give an error code to ensure that my Mini would get the right repair treatment.  The FAT partition doesn't take up a lot of space, and if you ever have to call Dell, it'll be good to have it.  I'd leave it on there.  :D

PS, if you use the Dell restore image, it'll put the FAT partition back on there.  Just FYI.

---

### Post by emptythevoid on 2009-03-06

> Ok, I installed the restricted codecs but the problem still remains. It seems that it take too much time to load fromn the CD. Ah only a thing. before the info about the tracks didn't appear. For example artist, title...

Are you using your own USB CD drive, or the one that Dell offers?  Maybe there's some kind of latency issue or something about the digital audio via USB that's not allowing it to play correctly.  

Also, have you tried any alternative programs to play your CDs?

### Post by ugm6hr on 2009-03-19
You cannot (at present) update to 8.10 without lots of potential problems - you have to reinstall 8.10 from scratch on the Mini.

As for the SD card issue - do they appear on the desktop when you plug them in?  What format are they?  Have to say, this sounds like a hardware issue, since Ubuntu should at least offer to mount any SD card automatically (Fat and Ext definitely).

---

### Post by liviubero on 2009-04-18
> **Dragonbite said:**
> Is that the sole machine you used for a while, or did you have to adjust going between a regular keyboard and the Mini's keyboard?

I use two K/Ubuntu machines. I didn't need to adjust. As sirebral just said, some keys are more difficult to reach (-, :, right shift)  and there is no F11 key, but it's alright. The keyboard is ok even when fast typing.
When I saw this keyboard for the first time, I thought that I will never be able to write anything on it, but after 5 minutes I forgot about it. After one hour intense typing, I had more problems with the size of the screen (I had to adjust my eyes to a bigger screen) as with the keyboard. But after one or two days I didn't had any problems anymore with that too.
If you can manage without a few keys, like F11, F12, the Menu-Key, then the keyboard will not be the main difficulty about Mini 9.

### Post by duckfeet on 2009-04-23
I got the Dell mini, and mine froze a couple times, but it *seemed* like it had something to do w/the touchpad, and I've had problems w/them before, w/laptops right out of the box, no matter *what* OS...

After I installed the touchpad tool in synaptics, and added a couple of things that had disappeared, which I found a thread on here about, my mini-9 has worked flawlessly...I *have* had problems, but they are kind of of my own making, as I'm a fanatic about removing stuff: I have 4gb ssd, and I've got 1.3 gb free.  I *had* 1.5 gb free...but I'd freed up a few things that needed to be kept in captivity...

As far as I'm concerned, comparing this to the Ubuntu 8.04 I had loaded on my home pc about a year ago...it's about the *same*...works good, just a matter of getting used to linux again...Dell's setup is o.k....it's a netbook, and I like the theory behind it....

### Post by duckfeet on 2009-04-25
No, I'm not sure: I just kind of searched around on here, and then when into 1st the apps remover, but they either wouldn't remove, of left too much, so used synaptics, as command line was just too much of a hassle, for me...to get out what I figured I wouldn't want, and I have my 4 gb mini down to 1.3 gb free space...

now, I removed cheese, like you did, and openoffice, and all the games, since all I need is a text editor, and also I removed evolution, as I use thunderbird, tho you want to be careful, as *one* of the evo files, (evolution-data), not the "big" one, also will remove gnome and your desktop, and then you can go thru some stress getting them back...I also took out some older kernels...and I use three cleanup tools, too, and got rid of orphans and stuff, and that got mine down really lean and mean, I'll go find the link to the good cleanup tools...here it is:

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=140920&highlight=cleanup+deborphan](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=140920&highlight=cleanup+deborphan)

I've broken my mini9 into 2 ext2 partitions (5.96 and 8.39 GiB; / and /home, respectively) and run without swap but a 2 gig RAM stick.  Using gparted, my "/" shows to be 2.75 Gig used (I've got 9.04 netbook remix installed plus kdebase, kdegames, and a few extra tools).

My disk is supposed to be a 16 gig SSD, but they are counting by 10^3, not 1024 to kilo, mega or giga so with partitioning, mbr, and such I only show 14.35 gig effective. 

I hope that this helps.
